    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3581161196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17179609411714997678">Everything is Always Gonna be Alright is a great book and message for young readers. A brilliant story to show children that no matter what your differences and the challenges that you face you can always get by with the help of friends. The book has a strong underlining message about diversity and acceptance as well as the importance of perseverance. The book also has some amazing illustrations and makes a great bedtime read. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3567830925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3567830925" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1362506-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442472304p2/1362506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3567830925?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3567830925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9758317247979599434">‘But I’m not special, and I can’t fly like every other bird’- honoring differences!<br/><br/>Virginia author Jamie McHone makes an impressive children’s book debut with EVERYTHING IS ALWAYS GONNA BE ALRIGHT, DURBAN FRANKENSHOOZE. The fine illustrations are by Walter Policelli. Jamie’s mission with this book – ‘to help children begin dialogues about diversity, acceptance and appreciation of differences, all while building vital language skills.’<br/><br/>For a children’s book the prose is sophisticated and for the y</span>
  <span id="freeText9758317247979599434" style="display:none">‘But I’m not special, and I can’t fly like every other bird’- honoring differences!<br /><br />Virginia author Jamie McHone makes an impressive children’s book debut with EVERYTHING IS ALWAYS GONNA BE ALRIGHT, DURBAN FRANKENSHOOZE. The fine illustrations are by Walter Policelli. Jamie’s mission with this book – ‘to help children begin dialogues about diversity, acceptance and appreciation of differences, all while building vital language skills.’<br /><br />For a children’s book the prose is sophisticated and for the younger set the story should be read aloud to them. Older children – elementary school age and beyond (meaning adults!) - will find the presentation informative as well as entertaining: the lyrical language is terrific.<br /><br />First the plot summary: ‘Durban is a Durban bird with giant sneakers and wings so small he can't fly. He's tired of being made fun of by all the other flying birds, so he sets off on a journey to find out who he really is. Along the way, he meets Maudry, a smart and sassy female bird, and Wainwright, a grumpy worm with a short temper. Together, the unusual trio goes through thick and thin to discover what it really means to be yourself.’<br /><br />For a taste of the joy of Jamie’s prose, the following is offered: ‘Durban Frankenshooze was a bird. A bird with tiny, ineffective wings. He did, however, seem to make up some appendage power in the fact that he had ginormous feet. So large that, at times, he got carried away and tripped headfirst into the earth. He would then have to pick himself up, dust himself off, pretend nothing was awry, and power on. But he had no choice because Durban couldn’t fly.’ And after his encounter with sassy bird Maudry, we learn, ‘Durban couldn’t believe that he had been so distracted by Maudry and her larger-than-life personality that he didn’t even think to inquire about what type of bird he was.’<br /><br />Using that charming writing style, Jamie introduces the concept of appreciating differences in others – and in ourselves! – that makes this a ‘children’s book for all ages!” Very highly recommended. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9758317247979599434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3034015678&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3034015678" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12363694022119877057">Durban Frankenshooze is an adorable Durban bird. Meaning he has enormous feet and cannot fly like his parents. One day he sets out to find another Durban bird. Instead he finds special friends who help him learn to love himself in spite of his perceived shortcomings.<br/><br/>I love the fun and clever names found in Everything is Always Gonna be Alright, Durban Frankenshooze. I love the focus on friendship and accepting friends and ourselves as fine just the way we/they are. Creative and engaging, this pi</span>
  <span id="freeText12363694022119877057" style="display:none">Durban Frankenshooze is an adorable Durban bird. Meaning he has enormous feet and cannot fly like his parents. One day he sets out to find another Durban bird. Instead he finds special friends who help him learn to love himself in spite of his perceived shortcomings.<br /><br />I love the fun and clever names found in Everything is Always Gonna be Alright, Durban Frankenshooze. I love the focus on friendship and accepting friends and ourselves as fine just the way we/they are. Creative and engaging, this picture book can be used for either a picture book or chapter book. The story is long for the youngest readers, but if broken into sections, it will work just fine. Older readers will be able to read this as a chapter book.<br /><br />Fun read, tons of new vocabulary and sayings, colorful illustrations, and a great theme. Readers will see that veryone is special in his or her own way and be encouraged to enjoy life and its adventures!</span>

  <span id="freeText2526286747884922848" style="display:none">Everything is always Gonna be Alright comes with a strong message about acceptance and diversity through the character Durban who is struggling with feeling different and disappointed in his abilities, or rather his inability to fly like everyone he knows can.<br />The book is very enjoyable to read to young children and will generate a lot of discussions. This is a great way to educate and bond with the children in your life but will require some patience as the language is rather advanced for such a young audience. Well worth the time though and a wonderful and necessary mentality to instil in kids. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3607371016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7697692503769668724">Durban Frankenshooze is a character for todays children. Durban goes through the challenges of not fitting in when all he wants is to be the same as everybody else. The book is designed to enlighten young children and show them the importance of being yourself and seeing the value in it. The book also has an advanced vocabulary for kids to pick up and also encourages lots of questions to enhance critical thinking. </span>

          </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1347779-breeann-she-just-loves-books?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3063419943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2104427066304127011">What I Loved: The illustrations in this book were great. They really pulled you into each page, wanting to take a look at each detail.<br/><br/>How I Felt: This book is targeted at 5-6 year olds, however, I do not think that the age range is accurate. Each page is filled with text taking so much time to read that my 6 year old lost interest. The writing introduces a lot of new vocabulary, but the text is overly fluffy, adding too many words. This just added to the overwhelming test on each page. The story</span>
  <span id="freeText2104427066304127011" style="display:none">What I Loved: The illustrations in this book were great. They really pulled you into each page, wanting to take a look at each detail.<br /><br />How I Felt: This book is targeted at 5-6 year olds, however, I do not think that the age range is accurate. Each page is filled with text taking so much time to read that my 6 year old lost interest. The writing introduces a lot of new vocabulary, but the text is overly fluffy, adding too many words. This just added to the overwhelming test on each page. The story was cute, but I cannot rate this book higher, as I cannot see a young child being able to get through this story. Overall, this book just missed the mark for me and my 6 year old.<br /><br />To Read or Not To Read: If you have a middle-elementary reader they might enjoy this story, but I would not suggest this for a 5-6 year old.<br /><br />What’s This Book About Anyway?<br />Durban Frankenschooze is a bird with huge feet and he cannot fly. He is different from the rest of his family, as he is the only bird that can’t fly. He is tired of being different and sets out on a journey. Along the way, he makes friends with Maudry and Wainwright. Together they discover the importance of friendship and being yourself.<br /><br />I received an advanced readers copy of this book for free. I am leaving this review voluntarily.<br /><br />All of my reviews can be found at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://shejustlovesbooks.com/">https://shejustlovesbooks.com/</a><br /></span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bHDzGax2wjusPS7OzheFaB8qn0RQvui43qJHYXTLVcdWVprLFygLUwsWmq854o+3yXV4jJ4zZt+F3AHQuYinXQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ouh1/+H/6ZhIrs0QgxOEGkRgEhe3aFMicOIpNRPaadqYzhwtWqEg8O+FeXF05o7Fkj/133nl3UUrnG+E3pmbQA==')})
  }
